| [Artemis VI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_VI "Artemis VI") |  | March 2031<sup id="cite_ref-fy25-m2m_17-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-fy25-m2m-17"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> | TBA | SLS Block 1B | TBA | ~30 days | Delivery of the [Crew and Science Airlock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crew_and_Science_Airlock_Module "Crew and Science Airlock Module") module to the Lunar Gateway, followed by a lunar landing. | Planned |

In November 2021, plans to return humans to the Moon in 2024 were cancelled, and the [Artemis III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_III "Artemis III") mission was delayed until at least 2025. It has since been delayed to mid-2027.<sup id="cite_ref-264"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-264"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup> Artemis VII is expected to deliver a crew of four astronauts to a [surface lunar outpost](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA_lunar_outpost_concepts "NASA lunar outpost concepts") known as the Foundation Habitat, along with the Mobile Habitat, which is expected to occur in March 2032.<sup id="cite_ref-sn-20230313_15-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-sn-20230313-15"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sep_2019_183-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-Sep_2019-183"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> The Foundation Habitat would be launched back to back with the Mobile Habitat by an undetermined super heavy launcher<sup id="cite_ref-Sep_2019_183-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-Sep_2019-183"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> and would be used for extended crewed lunar surface missions.<sup id="cite_ref-Sep_2019_183-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-Sep_2019-183"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-265"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arstechnica-plans_266-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-arstechnica-plans-266"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup>

Prior to each crewed Artemis mission, payloads to the [Gateway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Gateway "Lunar Gateway"), such as refueling depots and expendable elements of the lunar lander, would be deployed by commercial launch vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-spacecom-plans_267-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-spacecom-plans-267"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-arstechnica-plans_266-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-arstechnica-plans-266"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup> The most updated manifest includes missions suggested in NASA's timelines that have not been designed or funded from Artemis IV to IX.<sup id="cite_ref-govtribe-20211025_268-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-govtribe-20211025-268"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Foust_Aug2019_269-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-Foust_Aug2019-269"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sep_2019_183-4"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-Sep_2019-183"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_232-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-:1-232"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup>

| Mission | Launch date | Crew | Launch vehicle | Duration | Goal (proposed) |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Artemis VII | March 2032<sup id="cite_ref-fy25-m2m_17-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-fy25-m2m-17"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> | TBA | SLS Block 1B | ~30 days | Lunar landing with the delivery of the Habitable Mobility Platform ([Lunar Cruiser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Cruiser "Lunar Cruiser")) to the surface |
| Artemis VIII | 2033 | TBA | SLS Block 1B | ~60 days | Lunar landing with the delivery of lunar surface logistics and the Foundational Surface Habitat |
| Artemis IX | 2034 | TBA | SLS Block 2 | ~60 days | Lunar landing with the delivery of additional lunar surface logistics |
| Artemis X | 2035 (planned) | TBA | SLS Block 2 | <180 days | Lunar landing – a long-term stay with the delivery of lunar surface logistics |
| Artemis XI | 2036 (planned) | TBA | SLS Block 2 | ~365 days | Lunar living – Expansion of lunar surface base and crew shift<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> |

### Support missions schedule

\[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Artemis_program&action=edit&section=51 "Edit section: Support missions schedule")\]

Artemis support missions are robotic missions flown through the [CLPS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_Lunar_Payload_Services "Commercial Lunar Payload Services") program and [Gateway program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Gateway "Lunar Gateway"), and HLS demo and delivery missions.<sup id="cite_ref-Sep_2019_183-5"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-Sep_2019-183"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup>

1.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_ref-270 "Jump up")** All future dates in the table are NET

The Artemis program has received criticism from several space professionals.

Mark Whittington, who is a contributor to _[The Hill](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Hill_(newspaper) "The Hill (newspaper)")_ and an author of several space exploration studies, stated in an article that the "lunar orbit project doesn't help us get back to the Moon".<sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-284"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup>

Aerospace engineer, author, and [Mars Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Society "Mars Society") founder [Robert Zubrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Zubrin "Robert Zubrin") has voiced his distaste for the [Gateway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_Gateway "Lunar Gateway"), which is part of the Artemis program as of 2027. He presented an alternative approach to a 2024 crewed lunar landing called "Moon Direct", a successor to his proposed [Mars Direct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Direct "Mars Direct"). His vision phases out the SLS and Orion, replacing them with the [SpaceX launch vehicles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX_launch_vehicles "SpaceX launch vehicles") and [SpaceX Dragon 2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon_2 "SpaceX Dragon 2"). It proposes using a heavy ferry/lander that would be refueled on the lunar surface via [in situ resource utilization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/In_situ_resource_utilization "In situ resource utilization") and transfer the crew from LEO to the lunar surface. The concept bears a heavy resemblance to NASA's own [Space Transportation System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Transportation_System "Space Transportation System") proposal from the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-285"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup>

[Apollo 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") astronaut [Buzz Aldrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin "Buzz Aldrin") disagrees with NASA's current goals and priorities, including their plans for a lunar outpost. He questioned the benefit of the idea to "send a crew to an intermediate point in space, pick up a lander there and go down". However, Aldrin expressed support for Robert Zubrin's "Moon Direct" concept which involves lunar landers traveling from Earth orbit to the lunar surface and back.<sup id="cite_ref-spacenews_lunar-exploration-plans_286-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-spacenews_lunar-exploration-plans-286"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup>

The program attracted criticism for the fact that at least 15 launches will be required to refuel HLS in orbit per crewed mission.<sup id="cite_ref-287"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-287"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2024, SpaceX's Jennifer Jensen stated on a call that Starship HLS will require ten launches.<sup id="cite_ref-288"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_note-288"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup>

1.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_ref-10 "Jump up")** An Orion capsule was [flown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exploration_Flight_Test-1 "Exploration Flight Test-1") in 2014, but not the entire Orion spacecraft.
2.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_ref-13 "Jump up")** If an ancillary mission has already delivered Gateway to NRHO, HLS and Orion will dock to Gateway instead of to each other.

1.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_ref-NASA_OIG_2021_1-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_ref-NASA_OIG_2021_1-1) [NASA Office of Inspector General](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA_Office_of_Inspector_General "NASA Office of Inspector General") (15 November 2021). [NASA's Management of the Artemis Missions](https://oig.nasa.gov/docs/IG-22-003.pdf) (PDF) (Report). [NASA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA "NASA"). p. 21. Retrieved 18 January 2023. To account for all Artemis costs for FYs 2021 through 2025, including Phase 2 projects like the SLS Block 1B, Mobile Launcher 2, and Gateway, we found that $25 billion should be added to the Artemis Plan's estimated costs, increasing the total costs over this 5-year period to $53 billion. Furthermore, when considering the $40 billion already spent on the Artemis mission from FYs 2012 to 2020, the total projected cost through FY 2025 becomes $93 billion.

Retrieved 18 October 2018. ... selected but unspecified instruments from RP will instead be flown on future commercial lunar lander missions under a new Commercial Lunar Payload Services (CLPS) program. NASA released a draft request for proposals for that program April 27. \[...\] Under CLPS, NASA plans to issue multiple indefinite-delivery indefinite-quantity (IDIQ) contracts to companies capable of delivering payloads to the lunar surface. Companies would have to demonstrate their ability to land at least 10 kilograms of payload on the lunar surface by the end of 2021.

153.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemis_program#cite_ref-a3-1_156-0 "Jump up")** Weitering, Hanneke (23 May 2019). ["NASA Has a Full Plate of Lunar Missions Before Astronauts Can Return to Moon"](https://www.space.com/nasa-moon-missions-before-2024.html). Space.com. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20190525032714/https://www.space.com/nasa-moon-missions-before-2024.html) from the original on 25 May 2019. Retrieved 28 August 2019. And before NASA sends astronauts to the moon in 2024, the agency will first have to launch five aspects of the Gateway, all of which will be commercial vehicles that launch separately and join each other in lunar orbit. First, a power and propulsion element will launch in 2022. Then, the crew module will launch (without a crew) in 2023. In 2024, during the months leading up to the crewed landing, NASA will launch the last critical components: a transfer vehicle that will ferry landers from the Gateway to a lower lunar orbit, a descent module that will bring the astronauts to the lunar surface, and an ascent module that will bring them back up to the transfer vehicle, which will then return them to the Gateway.
